1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy Filter Chain Configuration Propagation

## Your Task

Trace how an Envoy HTTP filter configuration defined in a Protobuf `.proto` file in `envoyproxy/data-plane-api` gets consumed by the C++ filter implementation in `envoyproxy/envoy`. Find: 1. The `.proto` file in `data-plane-api` that defines the `HttpConnectionManager` filter chain configuration. 2. The C++ source files in `envoy` under `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/` that parse and apply this configuration. Report the repo, file path, and key type/class name for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

If the timeout fires, the stream\n562:   // is terminated with a 408 Request Timeout error code if no upstream response\n563:   // header has been received, otherwise a stream reset occurs.\n564:   //\n565:   // If the :ref:`overload action <config_overload_manager_overload_actions>` \"envoy.overload_actions.reduce_timeouts\"\n566:   // is configured, this timeout is scaled according to the value for\n567:   // :ref:`HTTP_DOWNSTREAM_STREAM_IDLE <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.overload.v3.ScaleTimersOverloadActionConfig.TimerType.HTTP_DOWNSTREAM_STREAM_IDLE>`.\n568:   //\n569:   // Note that it is possible to idle timeout even if the wire traffic for a stream is non-idle, due\n570:   // to the granularity of events presented to the connection manager. For example, while receiving\n571:   // very large request headers, it may be the case that there is traffic regularly arriving on the\n572:   // wire while the connection manage is only able to observe the end-of-headers event, hence the\n573:   // stream may still idle timeout.\n574:   //\n575:   // A value of 0 will completely disable the connection manager stream idle\n576:   // timeout, although per-route idle timeout overrides will continue to apply.\n577:   //\n578:   // This timeout is also used as the default value for :ref:`stream_flush_timeout\n579:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stream_flush_timeout>`.\n580:   google.protobuf.Duration stream_idle_timeout = 24\n581:       [(udpa.annotations.security).configure_for_untrusted_downstream = true];\n582: \n583:   // The stream flush timeout for connections managed by the connection manager.\n584:   //\n585:   // If not specified, the value of stream_idle_timeout is used. This is for backwards compatibility\n586:   // since this was the original behavior. In essence this timeout is an override for the\n587:   // stream_idle_timeout that applies specifically to the end of stream flush case.\n588:   //\n589:   // This timeout specifies the amount of time that Envoy will wait for the peer to open enough\n590:   // window to write any remaining stream data once the entirety of stream data (local end stream is\n591:   // true) has been buffered pending available window. In other words, this timeout defends against\n592:   // a peer that does not release enough window to completely write the stream, even though all\n593:   // data has been proxied within available flow control windows. If the timeout is hit in this\n594:   // case, the :ref:`tx_flush_timeout <config_http_conn_man_stats_per_codec>` counter will be\n595:   // incremented. Note that :ref:`max_stream_duration\n596:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HttpProtocolOptions.max_stream_duration>` does not apply to\n597:   // this corner case.\n598:   google.protobuf.Duration stream_flush_timeout = 59;\n599: \n600:   // The amount of time that Envoy will wait for the entire request to be received.\n601: ",
